#### What this PR does / why we need it:
KEP for #10189.

It introduces the implementation proposal for the MultiKueue Global Status Condition to track the true status of a Manage Workload in the MultiKueue environment throughout its lifetime.

#### Which issue(s) this PR fixes:
<!--
*Automatically closes linked issue when PR is merged.
Usage: `Fixes #<issue number>`, or `Fixes (paste link of issue)`.
_If PR is about `failing-tests or flakes`, please post the related issues/tests in a comment and do not use `Fixes`_*
-->
Addresses #10189

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:90** by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-04-08T07:34:17Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
+
+For each MultiKueueGlobalStatus a message - **MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage** - will be defined:
+* SUCCESS: `Workload has finished successfully on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* FAILED: `Workload failed after admission on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* WORKER_SELECTED: `Workload received quota reservation on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>. <number of ready admission checks>/<number of all admission checks> Admission Checks Ready.`
+* WAITING_FOR_WORKER:
+  * Default:
+  `Workload awaiting admission on one of the registered workers. <number of remotes> remotes created.`
+  * Non primary component workload:
+  `Component Workload awaiting admission on worker cluster: <worker nominated by the primary local workload>, nominated by <primary local workload reference>.`
```

  Should we make this distinction? Do the users even know what a "component workload" is?

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:84** by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-04-08T07:46:15Z

```diff
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
+
+For each MultiKueueGlobalStatus a message - **MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage** - will be defined:
+* SUCCESS: `Workload has finished successfully on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* FAILED: `Workload failed after admission on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
```

  Doesn't this duplicate information that already exists?
  
  Which makes me think if a condition like `AdmittedInWorker` that has the information about the MK replication process wouldn't "fit in" to the existing workload state rather than being an independent condition that contains everything.

### Review by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) (commented) — 2026-04-08T08:18:47Z

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:90** by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) — 2026-04-08T08:18:47Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
+
+For each MultiKueueGlobalStatus a message - **MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage** - will be defined:
+* SUCCESS: `Workload has finished successfully on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* FAILED: `Workload failed after admission on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* WORKER_SELECTED: `Workload received quota reservation on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>. <number of ready admission checks>/<number of all admission checks> Admission Checks Ready.`
+* WAITING_FOR_WORKER:
+  * Default:
+  `Workload awaiting admission on one of the registered workers. <number of remotes> remotes created.`
+  * Non primary component workload:
+  `Component Workload awaiting admission on worker cluster: <worker nominated by the primary local workload>, nominated by <primary local workload reference>.`
```

  We can omit the "component" keyword, but this distinction is important as the underlying logic is different to regular MK Workloads. We could name the job type instead of saying "compoinenet", e.g.
  `LeaderWorkerSet Workload awaiting admission... nominated by Primary LeaderWorkerSet Workload <id>.`

### Review by [@Singularity23x0](https://github.com/Singularity23x0) (commented) — 2026-04-08T08:27:23Z

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@

+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)

+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
+
+For each MultiKueueGlobalStatus a message - **MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage** - will be defined:
+* SUCCESS: `Workload has finished successfully on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* FAILED: `Workload failed after admission on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
```

  Then, once this condition is no longer needed, we loose the information that this workload is an MK one.
  
  The idea behind this condition is to make the workload status always be able to quickly identify an MK Workload and clearly relay what is happening to it. As running, failed and success are fundamentally different from what they are for an individual workload (e.g. finished-success for individual workload means the underlying job is finished, but it does not say whether it was finished locally or on a remote worker, nor which one specifically). The idea behind the differences of each of those statuses is expanded upon on the "Consolidated Workload State" section, focusing on contextual differences of each of those states.
  
  While I agree that the "INACTIVE" condition could be contested, other ones do always carry different information to what it "duplicates", as the context of MK in and of itself expands the meaning of these states/messages.

```diff
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
```

  We wouldn't lose the `AdmittedInWorker` condition, it would simply remain `True` with the proposed "Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>." message.
  
  And for "success" - how does it differ from `WorkloadFinished`? It should be kept in sync between the local workload and the running remote so there's not really a distinction of "whether it was finished locally or on a remote worker", no?

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:53** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-04-08T08:57:23Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
```

  What is "Distribution Strategy"? Did you mean "Dispatching"?

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:74** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-04-08T09:03:15Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
```

  ```suggestion
  this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in [#9338](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/issues/9338) occurs,
  ```
  
  AFAICS (in the preview) these #ids don't become links automatically in KEPs.
  
  And same below.

```diff
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").

+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.

+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
```

```diff
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
```

  Maybe it would be clearer to explicitly note here that our ultimate goal is to make this never happen?
  (Yet, it'll continue to be possible for some time, due to bug fixes rolling out behind feature gates).
  
  (Or do you think such an open claim is too strong / inaccurate?)

```diff
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
```

  The phrase "admitted (has the admitted condition)" appears here in a few places, which I find surprising.
  It seems you wish to avoid some ambiguity, but what kind of? And why with so many words?
  
  How about just "local workload is Admitted"? By capitalizing, you'd explicitly refer to the standard Kueue concept.

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:77** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-04-08T09:34:00Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
```

  Following up on [this comment](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/10266/changes#r3049824311), "component workload" might be unclear even for Kueue developers; e.g. it seems not to appear in any earlier KEP. 🫤 
  
  To clarify this, I'd propose to link e.g. [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8670#discussion_r2745488245); at least that's the nicest target I could find.

```diff
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
```

  "and waiting to nominate one of them" - is this accurate?
  
  * If it is, then we have a problem with names of states (because `WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION` is another state, not this one)
  * However, I think it isn't accurate. I think we just hit a _clash of notions_; see below.
  
  AFAICS the concept of "nominating" is used in Kueue in **two different meanings**:
  
  * One meaning refers to MK dispatcher _nominating_ worker clusters for dispatching remote workloads (see [MK KEP](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/keps/693-multikueue); also [KEP-8303](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/keps/8303-multikueue-orchestrated-preemption)).
    In that sense, we're no longer waiting for nomination here; nomination already happened.
    I think this is the meaning you used in the names of proposed states.
    I also think this is the dominant meaning, at least in recent months.
  
  * The other meaning is mostly found in the scheduler code (e.g. [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/b62584120f7f94cc01a2ed8d3afc5b340ec03a19/pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go#L478)) and also mentioned in some KEPs but just briefly (AFAICS [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/b62584120f7f94cc01a2ed8d3afc5b340ec03a19/keps/349-all-or-nothing/README.md?plain=1#L534) and [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/b62584120f7f94cc01a2ed8d3afc5b340ec03a19/keps/420-partial-admission/README.md?plain=1#L86)).
    I think this is the meaning you used when writing the descriptions of states here. (Not only this one; look around).
  
  Mixing both meanings leads to confusion.
  I propose to:
  
  * Remove all usages of "nominate" in "the scheduler meaning".
  * Link to MK KEP (e.g. [here](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/tree/main/keps/693-multikueue#multikueue-dispatcher-api)) to clarify what "nomination" means in this KEP.
  
  In particular, for this bullet, I'd propose this:
  
  ```suggestion
  * **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting for one of them to receive quota (upon which we'll graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state),
  ```

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:78** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-04-08T10:28:37Z

```diff
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
```

  Looking at it now, wouldn't `WAITING_FOR_MANAGER_QUOTA` be clearer?

- **keps/10189-multikueue-global-status-condition/README.md:109** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-04-08T10:31:58Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,293 @@
+# KEP-10189: MultiKueue Global Status Condition
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Notes/Constraints/Caveats](#notesconstraintscaveats)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+    - [e2e tests](#e2e-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Global Status Summary](#global-status-summary)
+  - [Visibility API](#visibility-api)
+  - [Consolidated Workload State](#consolidated-workload-state)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+The Workload status in queue in the MultiKueue Manager Cluster must reflect the true state of the workload derived from the remote cluster,
+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").
+
+This KEP focuses on a mechanism to provide such high-level summary in the form of a new Workload Status Condition - the **MultiKueueWorkload** condition.
+The condition:
+1. Will be populated for workloads created on the Manager Cluster.
+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Currently, the Workload Status subresource is missing key information aggregating data from across its remote counterparts on Worker Clusters.
+The existing conditions do not track the process of dispatching Remote Workloads to Workers, obstructing the details of MultiKueue's most critical part of the workload's execution.
+This forces users to search across all Worker Clusters to be able to see the big picture.
+
+Moreover, it does not natively support a contract defining a human-readable execution status.
+It instead relies on a list of Conditions and support information provided inside the WorkloadStatus field for the user to piece the actual global state of the underlying job's execution together on their own.
+
+To amend this, we need a way to present the user with a clearly defined, user-readable summary of the Global State, which aggregates information from across all the clusters of the MultiKueue environment.
+
+If nothing is implemented, the users will remain forced to rely on:
+* the conditions of the Manager Workload, which are misaligned and non-representative of all the extensive logic happening in MultiKueue,
+* manually querying and aggregating the conditions of Remote Workload across all Registered Workers; this covers a lot of distributed data; users are missing the core information of which Workers are eligible for distribution by virtue of being put forward by the Distribution Strategy.
+
+### Goals
+
+* Adding a new Workload Status Condition describing the current, actual state of the Manager Workload.
+* Defining an enumeration of mutually exclusive MultiKueue Manager Workload states covering the whole lifecycle of the workload.
+* Defining a set of high-level, human-readable messages to accompany the enumerated states, describing them further.
+* Populating the condition for relevant workloads.
+
+### Non-Goals
+
+* Defining Status Summary describing data structures beyond what's necessary for implementing the new Workload Status Condition.
+
+## Proposal
+
+The lifecycle of the Manager Workload will be split into the following **MultiKueueGlobalStatus** enumeration:
+* **SUCCESS** - workload finished successfully,
+* **FAILED** - workload finished with failed state,
+* **INACTIVE** - Manager Workload marked as inactive, preventing it from being scheduled; we can enter this state from any other as the workload can be deactivated both by Kueue and by the user,
+* **RUNNING** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a worker was nominated; the remote is admitted (has the admitted condition); the underlying job will attempt to execute; if it finishes we transition into the SUCCESS/FAILED state, otherwise we back-off,
+* **WORKER_SELECTED** - local workload is admitted (has the admitted condition); a single worker was nominated; the remote has currently received quota but is not admitted yet;
+this is possible if the MultiKueueWaitForWorkloadAdmitted feature is disabled; it can also occur as a consequence of graduating from the WAITING_FOR_WORKER state when the behavior described in  #9338  occurs,
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER** -  quota reserved on the local workload; dispatching remotes to eligible workers and waiting  to nominate one of them; a worker will be nominated once the remote achieves a state allowing it to graduate to either the WORKER_SELECTED or the RUNNING state,
+Note: Local workload can be admitted (have the admitted condition), as described in #9338 (when MultiKueue admits a workload on a worker but then it gets preempted there with the MultiKueueRedoAdmissionOnEvictionInWorker gate enabled).
+* **WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION** - specific to a non-primary component workload in the multi-workload-resource handling scenario;  quota reserved on the component workload; the component workload is waiting for the primary to nominate a worker to create a remote on,
+* **WAITING_FOR_QUOTA** - local workload is waiting to be granted a quota reservation on the Manager Cluster.
+
+For each MultiKueueGlobalStatus a message - **MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage** - will be defined:
+* SUCCESS: `Workload has finished successfully on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* FAILED: `Workload failed after admission on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* INACTIVE: `Workload inactive: <reason>.`
+* RUNNING: `Workload admitted on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>.`
+* WORKER_SELECTED: `Workload received quota reservation on worker cluster: <worker cluster reference>. <number of ready admission checks>/<number of all admission checks> Admission Checks Ready.`
+* WAITING_FOR_WORKER:
+  * Default:
+  `Workload awaiting admission on one of the registered workers. <number of remotes> remotes created.`
+  * Non primary component workload:
+  `Component Workload awaiting admission on worker cluster: <worker nominated by the primary local workload>, nominated by <primary local workload reference>.`
+* WAITING_FOR_WORKER_NOMINATION: `Component Workload waiting for <primary local workload reference> to nominate a worker cluster.`
+* WAITING_FOR_QUOTA: `Workload awaiting quota on the manager cluster.`
+
+The **MultiKueueWorkload** condition will be defined as:
+|Field|Value|
+|---|---|
+|Type|_MultiKueueWorkload_|
+|Status|_True_|
+|Reason|MultiKueueGlobalStatus|
+|Message|MultiKueueGlobalStatusMessage|
+
+The condition will be gated behind the **MultiKueueGlobalStatusCondition** feature gate.
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+
+I want to get an idea of when my job will be admitted. Has it already received quota on the manager?
+Is it being dispatched? If yes - what are the workers has it been dispatched to, so that I can check the status of some or all of them for how my job is doing there?
```

  ```suggestion
  Is it being dispatched? If yes - what are the workers it has been dispatched to, so that I can check the status of some or all of them for how my job is doing there?
  ```

```diff
+## Summary

+including a human-readable message explaining the state (e.g., "Waiting for quota in cluster X").

+1. Will provide a high-level, human-readable message explaining the state of the Manager Workload.
+1. Will provide insights into the Workload's progress throughout its **whole lifecycle**.
+1. Will aggregate the information from all the Remote Workloads dispatched by MultiKueue to Worker Clusters for the subject Manager Workload.
+
```
